This time it's an easy recipe but it's so fun to make that I thought everyone should know how to do it! I actually forgot about pop rice (or puffed rice) until recently when we had dinner at a hotel where they actually served it to us. I personally think pop rice on the stalk is the most fun of all, but of course if you don't have access to a rice paddy then you can make this with any raw rice at all from your grocery store.

I shall try this.  I believe I will try to make it the way popcorn is made, usually not deep fried.  The difference between popcorn and other varieties is that the skin on the popcorn kernel is not porous. The rapid build of steam from the moisture inside the kernel builds up enough pressure under the non porous skin, it explodes. So, I must also try this with brown rice to see the effect of the outer cover of the rice grain, to see if it pops more or less consistently than white rice. I have several varieties of rice in the cupboard.  This will be fun. Puffed barley is pretty interesting as well.

Actually, Indonesia kinda have it too. But it's a little different. We make it from rice and make like "hamburger" shape but loosely, not packed tight, and then we dried it under the sun until it theoretically harden and "turn back" into rice but with a shape, after that we fried it. It's called Rangginang. We usually made it from leftover rice.

Perfect! How about parboiled rice fried with a mix of milk butter/cleaned grease and rice bran oil? For someone want to reduce lipid: you can salt (the salt gives us the better thermal property than sand, an it will not make the pop food become saltier so much). However, I prefer your solution - frying. It gives us more fatty taste. In other way, we can use cold matured rice. We can separate mechanically, or use cold water to do it easier (and then we dry). Frying old (matured) rice gives us a equivalent puffed rice.

I really enjoy how you engage/involve your cats.  Some people say "cats are total jerks because, well.. that's just their nature." which is untrue not only for them, but for all pets. If you engage your pets, give them affection, and show them that they are part of your life, they will almost always react/behave accordingly.  For instance if you kick/yell at/isolate <insert_pet_here>, they will likely not react well to people. Alternatively, if you treat them as friends AKA engage them (pet them and talk to them) and also care for them (make ready their food and water), they will almost certainly love you and respect your (and their) surroundings.  Most of the time, the way a pet acts tends to be a reflection of yourself.  You get what you give :)

That's a quite common snack in Bangladesh. The rural areas it's like a daily snack. People here mostly incorporate this with spicy stuffs, which tastes pretty good actually. I personally prefer eating this with warm milk. Here it is known as "Khoi" we write it as "à¦–à¦‡". It's commonly known as "parched rice" in english if I'm not wrong. there's also "Muri" i. e. "à¦®à§à§œà¦¿"  which is known as puffed rice. Most people tends to get confused between these two.  Btw, that looks tasty! Gotta try it with chocolate someday ğŸ˜‡

Hey Jun, what portable stove do you use?
Here in Indonesia we have similar thing, but usually for home purpose, we use left-over cooked rice (that still good, of course) to make sure no food is wasted. We dry those rice under sun for 2-4 days (depends on the weather) and after it dries, we fry it just like you do. It can be eaten plain, or with some salt or sugar for seasoning. For business product purpose, I think it's inappropriate to use left-over, so maybe they use fresh rice and dry it under sun. It's kinda weird, you cook rice and then dry it under sun, and then fry it to make this food. But the benefit of cook-first-then-dry-and-fry is you can shape it when it's still soft, like, a round shape, it may be big or small to be a light snack while watching tv. We may use common rice found in market or sticky rice---which tastes better---and called it as "Rengginang".

HEY JUN CAN YOU MAKE MY RECIPE!!  SPECIAL UDON SOUP  Ingredients  Flour Salt Black pepper Other garnishes and seasonings of your liking Water Soy sauce Carrots Okra Chives Potatoes Celery Onio Eggs Shrimp Small bags Knife A Pot Bowls  Make Udon noodles  Sift flour into a bowl Dissolve salt into water Add the water to the flour And knead into dough Put the dough in a bag and step on it for as long as you want the longer to better Let it cure in a bag for about an hour Then cut it into noodles  Make the broth  Shred carrots Cut open okra so the center will be exposed for flavor Cut up shrimp Cut up onion into small pieces Add carrots, okra,Â  onion and shrimp in a pot of water and put it on medium heat until right before it boils Strain out ingredients for later use The left over water is the broth Add salt pepper and anything else you want to add  Cooking ingredients  Rub the hair of of the okra with salt Mince the onions Steam chives, potatoe chunks, carrots, onion, okra, shrimp and celery together with some soy sauce Chop the ingredients into small bits if needed Half boil an egg Cut half boiled egg in half  Construct meal  Put the ingredients in the broth Scoop the broth into a serving bowl Add the udon noodles Add half of a half boiled egg to the side Garnish with anything else you want Add any seasoning you want  ENJOY!  (Anyone can make this too obviously not just jun!)

I stumbled on this some 50yrs ago I fixed it for the kids for an after school snack and would not last more then 5min. I use a parboiled rice deep fry in veggie oil in a small pot 1 table spoon at a time on an electric stove for fear of fire using a tea leaf strainer, keep it covered if not it willÂ lose it's crunchÂ over night, it is best to use it ASAPÂ . It can still be used as regular cooked rice, just cook it in water as you would any rice, I have used it in cakes, cookies, salads, ice cream topping, in cake frosting,Â  as for the kids I used "popcorn sault " to give it a popcorn taste. 1 cup of rice would yelled about 2 cups by volume. Hope you all enjoy

You donâ€™t need oil if youâ€™re watching your calories. You can pop rice in hot salt. Use pure salt without any additives. The finer the better. You need enough of it to bury all the rice or corn without losing too much heat. Heat it up in an oven, take it out, quickly add the rice, close the lid, shake, wait a few seconds till it pops, sift it, put the salt back into the oven, and repeat.

JUN if you want your chocolate to look shiny on the outside like the one right out of the box than you need it to have the right temperature. That usually means to melt the chocolate at around 30-35 â„ƒ , to than let it cool to around 27â„ƒ . At that temperature small crystals for inside the chocolate. Afterwards you warm it up again to around 32â„ƒ (that way those crystals don't melt yet but stay intact while the chocolate is more runny). Now you can glaze with it or make your little sweets :D

First
This time it's an easy recipe but it's so fun to make that I thought everyone should know how to do it! I actually forgot about pop rice (or puffed rice) until recently when we had dinner at a hotel where they actually served it to us. I personally think pop rice on the stalk is the most fun of all, but of course if you don't have access to a rice paddy then you can make this with any raw rice at all from your grocery store.
